<p><b>Wind power</b> or <b>wind energy</b> is mostly the use of <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a> to <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generate electricity</a>. Wind power is a popular, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> source that has a much smaller <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_wind_power" title="Environmental impact of wind power">impact on the environment</a> than burning <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>. Historically, wind power has been used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sails" title="Sails">sails</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windpump" title="Windpump">windpumps</a> but today it is mostly used to generate electricity. <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">Wind farms</a> consist of many individual wind turbines, which are connected to the <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">electric power transmission</a> <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">network</a>.
</p><p>New <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Onshore_wind_farm" title="Onshore wind farm">onshore (on-land) wind farms</a> are cheaper than new  <a href="/wiki/Coal-fired_power_station" title="Coal-fired power station">coal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Gas-fired_power_plant" title="Gas-fired power plant">gas plants</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-1">[1]</a></sup> but expansion of wind power is being hindered by <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">fossil fuel subsidies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-4">[4]</a></sup> Onshore wind farms have a greater visual <a href="#Impact_on_environment_and_landscape">impact on the landscape</a> than some other power stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grantham_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-grantham-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energyfootprint_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-energyfootprint-6">[6]</a></sup> Small onshore wind farms can feed some energy into the grid or provide power to isolated off-grid locations. <a href="/wiki/Offshore_wind_power" title="Offshore wind power">Offshore wind farms</a> provide a steadier and stronger source of energy and have less visual impact. Although there is less offshore wind power at present and construction and maintenance costs are higher, it is expanding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wind power is <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">variable renewable energy</a>, so <a href="/wiki/Energy_management" title="Energy management">power-management</a> techniques are used to match supply and demand, such as: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_hybrid_power_systems" title="Wind hybrid power systems">wind hybrid power systems</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" title="Hydroelectric power">hydroelectric power</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable</a> power sources, excess capacity, geographically distributed turbines, exporting and importing power to neighboring areas, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grid_storage" title="Grid storage">grid storage</a>. As the proportion of wind power in a region increases the grid may need to be upgraded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ieawind_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ieawind-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abbess_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-abbess-9">[9]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weather_forecast" title="Weather forecast">Weather forecasting</a> allows the electric-power network to be readied for the predictable variations in production that occur.
</p><p>In 2021, wind supplied over 1800 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TWh" title="TWh">TWh</a> of electricity, which was over 6% of world electricity<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and about 2% of world energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpcom_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpcom-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup> With about 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigawatt" title="Gigawatt">GW</a> added during 2021, mostly <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_China" title="Wind power in China">in China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_the_United_States" title="Wind power in the United States">United States</a>, global installed wind power capacity exceeded 800 GW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> To help meet the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> goals to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">limit climate change</a>, analysts say it should expand much faster - by over 1% of electricity generation per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_energy">Wind energy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1092" data-file-width="2488" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png/350px-Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png/525px-Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png/700px-Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_Map_of_Wind_Speed.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global map of wind speed at 100 m above surface level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_wind_atlas_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-global_wind_atlas-15">[15]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="2871" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/350px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/525px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/700px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roscoe_Wind_Farm" title="Roscoe Wind Farm">Roscoe Wind Farm</a>: an onshore wind farm in <a href="/wiki/West_Texas" title="West Texas">West Texas</a> near <a href="/wiki/Roscoe,_Texas" title="Roscoe, Texas">Roscoe</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg/350px-Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg/525px-Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg/700px-Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lee_Ranch_Wind_Speed_Frequency.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of wind speed (red) and energy (blue) for all of 2002 at the Lee Ranch facility in Colorado. The histogram shows measured data, while the curve is the Rayleigh model distribution for the same average wind speed.</div></div></div>
<p>Wind energy is the <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> of air in motion, also called <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">wind</a>.
Total wind energy flowing through an imaginary surface with area <i>A</i> during the time <i>t</i> is:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E={\frac {1}{2}}mv^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}(Avt\rho )v^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}At\rho v^{3},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E={\frac {1}{2}}mv^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}(Avt\rho )v^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}At\rho v^{3},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E={\frac {1}{2}}mv^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}(Avt\rho )v^{2}={\frac {1}{2}}At\rho v^{3}," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/768a83c369a7213461cfe88536d02e52d8a1a850" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:36.806ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physics_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-physics-16">[16]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>where <i>ρ</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Density_of_air" title="Density of air">density of air</a>; <i>v</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Wind_speed" title="Wind speed">wind speed</a>; <i>Avt</i> is the volume of air passing through <i>A</i> (which is considered perpendicular to the direction of the wind); <i>Avtρ</i> is therefore the mass <i>m</i> passing through A. ½ <i>ρv</i><sup>2</sup> is the kinetic energy of the moving air per unit volume.
</p><p>Power is energy per unit time, so the wind power incident on <i>A</i> (e.g. equal to the rotor area of a wind turbine) is:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P={\frac {E}{t}}={\frac {1}{2}}A\rho v^{3}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>P</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>E</mi>
<mi>t</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mn>2</mn>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mi>A</mi>
<mi>ρ<!-- ρ --></mi>
<msup>
<mi>v</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P={\frac {E}{t}}={\frac {1}{2}}A\rho v^{3}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P={\frac {E}{t}}={\frac {1}{2}}A\rho v^{3}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/30739560fad0d0b3435acd7a9acdc0ae045e7306" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:18.326ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physics_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-physics-16">[16]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Wind power in an open air stream is thus <i>proportional</i> to the <i>third power</i> of the wind speed; the available power increases eightfold when the wind speed doubles.
</p><p>Wind is the movement of air across the surface of the Earth, driven by areas of high and low pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
The global wind kinetic energy averaged approximately 1.50 MJ/m<sup>2</sup> over the period from 1979 to 2010, 1.31 MJ/m<sup>2</sup> in the Northern Hemisphere with 1.70 MJ/m<sup>2</sup> in the Southern Hemisphere. The atmosphere acts as a thermal engine, absorbing heat at higher temperatures, releasing heat at lower temperatures. The process is responsible for the production of wind kinetic energy at a rate of 2.46 W/m<sup>2</sup> thus sustaining the circulation of the atmosphere against friction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Through <a href="/wiki/Wind_resource_assessment" title="Wind resource assessment">wind resource assessment</a> it is possible to estimate wind power potential globally, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_by_country" title="Wind power by country">by country</a> or region, or for a specific site. The <a href="/wiki/Global_Wind_Atlas" title="Global Wind Atlas">Global Wind Atlas</a> provided by the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Denmark" title="Technical University of Denmark">Technical University of Denmark</a> in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> provides a global assessment of wind power potential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_wind_atlas_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-global_wind_atlas-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
Unlike 'static' wind resource atlases which average estimates of wind speed and power density across multiple years, tools such as <a href="/wiki/Renewables.ninja" title="Renewables.ninja">Renewables.ninja</a> provide time-varying simulations of wind speed and power output from different wind turbine models at an hourly resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> More detailed, site-specific assessments of wind resource potential can be obtained from specialist commercial providers, and many of the larger wind developers have in-house modeling capabilities.
</p><p>The total amount of economically extractable power available from the wind is considerably more than present human power use from all sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The strength of wind varies, and an average value for a given location does not alone indicate the amount of energy a wind turbine could produce there.
</p><p>To assess prospective wind power sites a probability distribution function is often fit to the observed wind speed data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Different locations will have different wind speed distributions. The <a href="/wiki/Weibull_distribution" title="Weibull distribution">Weibull</a> model closely mirrors the actual distribution of hourly/ten-minute wind speeds at many locations. The Weibull factor is often close to 2 and therefore a <a href="/wiki/Rayleigh_distribution" title="Rayleigh distribution">Rayleigh distribution</a> can be used as a less accurate, but simpler model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_farms">Wind farms</span></h2>

<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muppandal_wind_farm" title="Muppandal wind farm">Muppandal wind farm</a></td>
<td align="center">1,500</td>
<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>India</td>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Alta_Wind_Energy_Center" title="Alta Wind Energy Center">Alta (Oak Creek-Mojave)</a></td>
<td align="center">1,320</td>
<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>United States</td>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Jaisalmer_Wind_Park" title="Jaisalmer Wind Park">Jaisalmer Wind Park</a></td>
<td align="center">1,064</td>
<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1350" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>India</td>
<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A wind farm is a group of <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a> in the same location. A large wind farm may consist of several hundred individual wind turbines distributed over an extended area. The land between the turbines may be used for agricultural or other purposes. For example, <a href="/wiki/Gansu_Wind_Farm" title="Gansu Wind Farm">Gansu Wind Farm</a>, the largest wind farm in the world, has several thousand turbines. A wind farm may also be located offshore. Almost all large wind turbines have the same design — a horizontal axis wind turbine having an upwind rotor with 3 blades, attached to a <a href="/wiki/Nacelle_(wind_turbine)" title="Nacelle (wind turbine)">nacelle</a> on top of a tall tubular tower.
</p><p>In a wind farm, individual turbines are interconnected with a medium voltage (often 34.5 kV) power collection system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and communications network. In general, a distance of 7D (7 times the rotor diameter of the wind turbine) is set between each turbine in a fully developed wind farm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> At a substation, this medium-voltage electric current is increased in voltage with a <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformer</a> for connection to the high voltage <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">electric power transmission</a> system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generator_characteristics_and_stability">Generator characteristics and stability</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Induction_generator" title="Induction generator">Induction generators</a>, which were often used for wind power projects in the 1980s and 1990s, require <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reactive_power" title="Reactive power">reactive power</a> for <a href="/wiki/Excitation_(magnetic)" title="Excitation (magnetic)">excitation</a>, so <a href="/wiki/Electrical_substation" title="Electrical substation">electrical substations</a> used in wind-power collection systems include substantial <a href="/wiki/Capacitor" title="Capacitor">capacitor</a> banks for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_factor_correction" title="Power factor correction">power factor correction</a>. Different types of wind turbine generators behave differently during transmission grid disturbances, so extensive modeling of the dynamic electromechanical characteristics of a new wind farm is required by transmission system operators to ensure predictable stable behavior during system faults (see <a href="/wiki/Wind_energy_software" title="Wind energy software">wind energy software</a>). In particular, induction generators cannot support the system voltage during faults.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Induction generators are not used in current turbines. Instead, most turbines use variable speed generators combined with either a partial or full-scale power converter between the turbine generator and the collector system, which generally have more desirable properties for grid interconnection and have <a href="/wiki/Low_voltage_ride_through" title="Low voltage ride through">low voltage ride through</a>-capabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-huang-32">[32]</a></sup> Modern turbines use either <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doubly_fed_electric_machine" title="Doubly fed electric machine">doubly fed electric machines</a> with partial-scale converters or squirrel-cage induction generators or synchronous generators (both permanently and electrically excited) with full-scale converters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Black_start" title="Black start">Black start</a> is possible<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and is being further developed for places (such as <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>) which generate most of their electricity from wind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Transmission_system_operator" title="Transmission system operator">Transmission systems operators</a> will supply a wind farm developer with a <a href="/wiki/Grid_code" title="Grid code">grid code</a> to specify the requirements for interconnection to the transmission grid. This will include the <a href="/wiki/Power_factor" title="Power factor">power factor</a>, the constancy of <a href="/wiki/Utility_frequency" title="Utility frequency">frequency</a>, and the dynamic behaviour of the wind farm turbines during a system fault.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offshore_wind_power">Offshore wind power</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Offshore_wind_power" title="Offshore wind power">Offshore wind power</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_offshore_wind_farms" title="List of offshore wind farms">List of offshore wind farms</a></div>
<p>Offshore wind power is wind farms in large bodies of water, usually the sea. These installations can utilize the more frequent and powerful winds that are available in these locations and have less visual impact on the landscape than land-based projects. However, the construction and maintenance costs are considerably higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vestas" title="Vestas">Vestas</a> are the leading turbine suppliers for offshore wind power. <a href="/wiki/%C3%98rsted_(company)" title="Ørsted (company)">Ørsted</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vattenfall" title="Vattenfall">Vattenfall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a> are the leading offshore operators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btm2010o_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-btm2010o-41">[41]</a></sup> As of November 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Hornsea_Wind_Farm" title="Hornsea Wind Farm">Hornsea Wind Farm</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> is the largest offshore wind farm in the world at 1,218 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatt" title="Megawatt">MW</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hornsea_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-hornsea-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collection_and_transmission_network">Collection and transmission network</span></h3>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farm</a>, individual turbines are interconnected with a medium voltage (usually 34.5 kV) power collection system and communications network. At a substation, this medium-voltage electric current is increased in voltage with a transformer for connection to the high voltage <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">electric power transmission</a> system. A transmission line is required to bring the generated power to (often remote) markets. For an offshore station, this may require a submarine cable. Construction of a new high voltage line may be too costly for the wind resource alone, but wind sites may take advantage of lines already installed for conventional fuel generation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Wind power resources are not always located near to high population density. As transmission lines become longer the losses associated with power transmission increase, as modes of losses at lower lengths are exacerbated and new modes of losses are no longer negligible as the length is increased, making it harder to transport large loads over large distances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the transmission capacity does not meet the generation capacity, wind farms are forced to produce below their full potential or stop running altogether, in a process known as <a href="/wiki/Curtailment_(electricity)" title="Curtailment (electricity)">curtailment</a>. While this leads to potential renewable generation left untapped, it prevents possible grid overload or risk to reliable service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maine_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-maine-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the biggest current challenges to wind power grid integration in some countries is the necessity of developing new transmission lines to carry power from wind farms, usually in remote lowly populated areas due to availability of wind, to high load locations, usually on the coasts where population density is higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Any existing transmission lines in remote locations may not have been designed for the transport of large amounts of energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-46">[46]</a></sup> In particular geographic regions, peak wind speeds may not coincide with peak demand for electrical power, whether offshore or onshore. A possible future option may be to interconnect widely dispersed geographic areas with an HVDC <a href="/wiki/Super_grid" title="Super grid">super grid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_power_capacity_and_production">Wind power capacity and production</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_by_country" title="Wind power by country">Wind power by country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_industry" title="Wind power industry">Wind power industry</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_trends">Growth trends</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:-moz-fit-content; width:-webkit-fit-content; width:fit-content;"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:auto;">
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1039153519">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" data-graph-id="692cd2a45c60083638ed94b2aaf0246cbae339b5" style="min-width:290px;min-height:200px"></div></div><div class="thumbcaption">Log graph of global wind power cumulative capacity (Data:GWEC)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GWEC_Market_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-GWEC_Market-48">[48]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_energy_generation_by_region,_OWID.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg/370px-Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg/555px-Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg/740px-Wind_energy_generation_by_region%2C_OWID.svg.png 2x" width="370"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_energy_generation_by_region,_OWID.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wind energy generation by region over time<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 2020, wind supplied almost 1600 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TWh" title="TWh">TWh</a> of electricity, which was over 5% of worldwide electrical generation and about 2% of energy consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpcom_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-bpcom-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup> With over 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigawatt" title="Gigawatt">GW</a> added during 2020, mostly <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_China" title="Wind power in China">in China</a>, global installed wind power capacity reached more than 730 GW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup> But to help meet <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> goals to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">limit climate change</a> analysts say it should expand much faster - by over 1% of electricity generation per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14">[14]</a></sup> Expansion of wind power is being hindered by <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">fossil fuel subsidies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>The actual amount of electric power that wind can generate is calculated by multiplying the <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">nameplate capacity</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Capacity_factor" title="Capacity factor">capacity factor</a>, which varies according to equipment and location.
Estimates of the capacity factors for wind installations are in the range of 35% to 44%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_generation_by_country.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Wind_generation_by_country.svg/220px-Wind_generation_by_country.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Wind_generation_by_country.svg/330px-Wind_generation_by_country.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Wind_generation_by_country.svg/440px-Wind_generation_by_country.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_generation_by_country.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wind generation by country</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capacity_factor">Capacity factor</span></h3>
<p>Since wind speed is not constant, a wind farm's annual <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> production is never as much as the sum of the generator nameplate ratings multiplied by the total hours in a year. The ratio of actual productivity in a year to this theoretical maximum is called the <a href="/wiki/Capacity_factor" title="Capacity factor">capacity factor</a>. Online data is available for some locations, and the capacity factor can be calculated from the yearly output.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MassMaritime_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-MassMaritime-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iesoOntarioWind_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-iesoOntarioWind-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike fueled generating plants, the capacity factor is affected by several parameters, including the variability of the wind at the site and the size of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_generator" title="Electric generator">generator</a> relative to the turbine's swept area. A small generator would be cheaper and achieve a higher capacity factor but would produce less <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a> (and thus less profit) in high winds. Conversely, a large generator would cost more but generate little extra power and, depending on the type, may <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stall_(flight)" title="Stall (flight)">stall</a> out at low wind speed. Thus an optimum capacity factor of around 40–50% would be aimed for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capacity-factor-50_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-capacity-factor-50-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capFactors_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-capFactors-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>

1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/20220824_Share_of_electricity_generated_by_wind_power%2C_by_country_-_Ember_Review.svg/442px-20220824_Share_of_electricity_generated_by_wind_power%2C_by_country_-_Ember_Review.svg.png 2x" width="221"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">In 2021, <a class="mw-selflink selflink">wind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar</a> power reached a record 10% of global electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ember_20220330_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ember_20220330-55">[55]</a></sup> Shown: 20 leading countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmberElectricityReview_202203_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmberElectricityReview_202203-56">[56]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Wind energy penetration is the fraction of energy produced by wind compared with the total generation. Wind power's share of worldwide electricity usage in 2021 was almost 7%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> up from 3.5% in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is no generally accepted maximum level of wind penetration. The limit for a particular <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">grid</a> will depend on the existing generating plants, pricing mechanisms, capacity for <a href="/wiki/Energy_storage" title="Energy storage">energy storage</a>, demand management, and other factors. An interconnected electric power grid will already include <a href="/wiki/Operating_reserve" title="Operating reserve">reserve generating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission#Capacity" title="Electric power transmission">transmission capacity</a> to allow for equipment failures. This reserve capacity can also serve to compensate for the varying power generation produced by wind stations. Studies have indicated that 20% of the total annual electrical energy consumption may be incorporated with minimal difficulty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tacklingUS_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-tacklingUS-60">[60]</a></sup> These studies have been for locations with geographically dispersed wind farms, some degree of <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable energy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> with storage capacity, demand management, and interconnected to a large grid area enabling the export of electric power when needed. Beyond the 20% level, there are few technical limits, but the economic implications become more significant. Electrical utilities continue to study the effects of large-scale penetration of wind generation on system stability<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and economics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minnesota_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-minnesota-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESB2004Study_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESB2004Study-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinclairMerz_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-sinclairMerz-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (January 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>A wind energy penetration figure can be specified for different duration of time but is often quoted annually. To obtain 100% from wind annually requires substantial long-term storage or substantial interconnection to other systems that may already have substantial storage. On a monthly, weekly, daily, or hourly basis—or less—wind might supply as much as or more than 100% of current use, with the rest stored, exported or curtailed. The seasonal industry might then take advantage of high wind and low usage times such as at night when wind output can exceed normal demand. Such industry might include the production of silicon, aluminum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> steel, or natural gas, and hydrogen, and using future long-term storage to facilitate 100% energy from <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">variable renewable energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Homes can also be programmed to accept extra electric power on demand, for example by remotely turning up water heater thermostats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Variability">Variability</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy" title="Variable renewable energy">Variable renewable energy</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Grid_balancing" title="Grid balancing">Grid balancing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toro_de_osborne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2538" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Toro_de_osborne.jpg/220px-Toro_de_osborne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Toro_de_osborne.jpg/330px-Toro_de_osborne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Toro_de_osborne.jpg/440px-Toro_de_osborne.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toro_de_osborne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wind turbines are typically installed in windy locations. In the image, wind power <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Spain" title="Wind power in Spain">generators in Spain</a>, near an <a href="/wiki/Osborne_bull" title="Osborne bull">Osborne bull</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="2871" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/220px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/330px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg/440px-Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_Wind_Farm_in_West_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roscoe Wind Farm in West Texas</div></div></div>
<p>Wind power is variable, and during low wind periods, it may need to be replaced by other power sources. Transmission networks presently cope with outages of other generation plants and daily changes in electrical demand, but the variability of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intermittent_power_source" title="Intermittent power source">intermittent power sources</a> such as wind power is more frequent than those of conventional power generation plants which, when scheduled to be operating, may be able to deliver their nameplate capacity around 95% of the time.
</p><p>Electric power generated from wind power can be highly variable at several different timescales: hourly, daily, or seasonally. Annual variation also exists but is not as significant.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Because instantaneous electrical generation and consumption must remain in balance to maintain grid stability, this variability can present substantial challenges to incorporating large amounts of wind power into a grid system. Intermittency and the non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intermittent_power_sources#Terminology" title="Intermittent power sources">dispatchable</a> nature of wind energy production can raise costs for regulation, incremental <a href="/wiki/Operating_reserve" title="Operating reserve">operating reserve</a>, and (at high penetration levels) could require an increase in the already existing <a href="/wiki/Energy_demand_management" title="Energy demand management">energy demand management</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Load_shedding" title="Load shedding">load shedding</a>, storage solutions, or system interconnection with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_voltage_direct_current" title="High voltage direct current">HVDC</a> cables.
</p><p>Fluctuations in load and allowance for the failure of large fossil-fuel generating units require operating reserve capacity, which can be increased to compensate for the variability of wind generation.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Battery_storage_power_station" title="Battery storage power station">Utility-scale batteries</a> are often used to balance hourly and shorter timescale variation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">car batteries</a> may gain ground from the mid-2020s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Wind power advocates argue that periods of low wind can be dealt with by simply restarting existing power stations that have been held in readiness, or interlinking with HVDC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Czisch-Giebel_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Czisch-Giebel-72">[72]</a></sup> Electrical grids with slow-responding thermal power plants and without ties to networks with hydroelectric generation may have to limit the use of wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denmark_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (September 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The combination of diversifying variable renewables by type and location, forecasting their variation, and integrating them with dispatchable renewables, flexible fueled generators, and demand response can create a power system that has the potential to meet power supply needs reliably. Integrating ever-higher levels of renewables is being successfully demonstrated in the real world:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In 2009, eight American and three European authorities, writing in the leading electrical engineers' professional journal, didn't find "a credible and firm technical limit to the amount of wind energy that can be accommodated by electric power grids". In fact, not one of more than 200 international studies, nor official studies for the eastern and western U.S. regions, nor the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>, has found major costs or technical barriers to reliably integrating up to 30% variable renewable supplies into the grid, and in some studies much more.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="920" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png/220px-Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png/330px-Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png/440px-Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seasonal_cycle_of_capacity_factors_for_wind_and_photovoltaics_in_Europe_under_idealized_assumptions.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seasonal cycle of capacity factors for wind and photovoltaics in Europe under idealized assumptions. The figure illustrates the balancing effects of wind and solar energy at the seasonal scale (Kaspar et al., 2019).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balancing-europe_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-balancing-europe-75">[75]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">Solar power</a> tends to be complementary to wind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-windsun_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-windsun-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smallWindSystems_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-smallWindSystems-77">[77]</a></sup> On daily to weekly timescales, <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">high-pressure areas</a> tend to bring clear skies and low surface winds, whereas <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure areas</a> tend to be windier and cloudier. On seasonal timescales, solar energy peaks in summer, whereas in many areas wind energy is lower in summer and higher in winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[A]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cleveland_water_crib_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland_water_crib-79">[78]</a></sup> Thus the seasonal variation of wind and solar power tend to cancel each other somewhat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balancing-europe_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-balancing-europe-75">[75]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_hybrid_power_systems" title="Wind hybrid power systems">Wind hybrid power systems</a> are becoming more popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Predictability">Predictability</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_forecasting" title="Wind power forecasting">Wind power forecasting</a></div>
<p>Wind power forecasting methods are used, but the predictability of any particular wind farm is low for short-term operation. For any particular generator, there is an 80% chance that wind output will change less than 10% in an hour and a 40% chance that it will change 10% or more in 5 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>In summer 2021 <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Wind power in the United Kingdom">wind power in the United Kingdom</a> fell due to the lowest winds in seventy years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> - smoothing peaks by <a href="/wiki/Green_hydrogen" title="Green hydrogen">producing hydrogen</a> may help in future when wind has a larger share of generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the output from a single turbine can vary greatly and rapidly as local wind speeds vary, as more turbines are connected over larger and larger areas the average power output becomes less variable and more predictable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-huang-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weather_forecast" title="Weather forecast">Weather forecasting</a> permits the electric-power network to be readied for the predictable variations in production that occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is thought that the most reliable low-carbon electricity systems will include a large share of wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_storage">Energy storage</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">Grid energy storage</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_energy_storage_projects" title="List of energy storage projects">List of energy storage projects</a></div><p>Typically, conventional <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> complements wind power very well. When the wind is blowing strongly, nearby hydroelectric stations can temporarily hold back their water. When the wind drops they can, provided they have the generation capacity, rapidly increase production to compensate. This gives a very even overall power supply and virtually no loss of energy and uses no more water.
</p><p>Alternatively, where a suitable head of water is not available, <a href="/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity" title="Pumped-storage hydroelectricity">pumped-storage hydroelectricity</a> or other forms of <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid energy storage</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compressed_air_energy_storage" title="Compressed air energy storage">compressed air energy storage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage" title="Thermal energy storage">thermal energy storage</a> can store energy developed by high-wind periods and release it when needed. The type of storage needed depends on the wind penetration level – low penetration requires daily storage, and high penetration requires both short- and long-term storage – as long as a month or more.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Stored energy increases the economic value of wind energy since it can be shifted to displace higher-cost generation during peak demand periods. The potential revenue from this <a href="/wiki/Arbitrage" title="Arbitrage">arbitrage</a> can offset the cost and losses of storage. Although pumped-storage power systems are only about 75% efficient, and have high installation costs, their low running costs and ability to reduce the required electrical base-load can save both fuel and total electrical generation costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinorwig_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-dinorwig-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-futureStorage_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-futureStorage-88">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_savings_and_energy_payback">Fuel savings and energy payback</span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Wind_Energy_Association" title="American Wind Energy Association">American Wind Energy Association</a>, production of wind power in the United States in 2015 avoided consumption of 280 million cubic metres (73 billion US gallons) of water and reduced CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> emissions by 132 million metric tons, while providing US$7.3 bn in public health savings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>The energy needed to build a wind farm divided into the total output over its life, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_Return_on_Energy_Invested" title="Energy Return on Energy Invested">Energy Return on Energy Invested</a>, of wind power varies but averages about 20–25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Thus, the energy payback time is typically around a year.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Onshore-wind-lcoe.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3400" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Onshore-wind-lcoe.png/310px-Onshore-wind-lcoe.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Onshore-wind-lcoe.png/465px-Onshore-wind-lcoe.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Onshore-wind-lcoe.png/620px-Onshore-wind-lcoe.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Onshore-wind-lcoe.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Onshore wind cost per kilowatt-hour between 1983 and 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Onshore wind is an inexpensive source of electric power, cheaper than coal plants and new gas plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-1">[1]</a></sup> According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BusinessGreen" title="BusinessGreen">BusinessGreen</a>, wind turbines reached <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">grid parity</a> (the point at which the cost of wind power matches traditional sources) in some areas of Europe in the mid-2000s, and in the US around the same time. Falling prices continue to drive the Levelized cost down and it has been suggested that it has reached general grid parity in Europe in 2010, and will reach the same point in the US around 2016 due to an expected reduction in capital costs of about 12%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessgreen_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessgreen-94">[93]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (September 2022)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2021 the CEO of <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Gamesa" title="Siemens Gamesa">Siemens Gamesa</a> warned that increased demand for low-cost wind turbines combined with high input costs and high costs of steel result in increased pressure on the manufacturers and decreasing profit margins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>Northern Eurasia, Canada, some parts of the United States, and <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a> in Argentina are the best areas for onshore wind: whereas in other parts of the world solar power, or a combination of wind and solar, tend to be cheaper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 8">: 8 </span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_power_cost_and_trends">Electric power cost and trends</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/220px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/330px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg/440px-Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turbine_Blade_Convoy_Passing_through_Edenfield.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A turbine blade convoy passing through <a href="/wiki/Edenfield" title="Edenfield">Edenfield</a> in the U.K. (2008). Even longer <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Blade_design" title="Wind turbine design">2-piece blades</a> are now manufactured, and then assembled on-site to reduce difficulties in transportation.</div></div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_electricity_by_source" title="Cost of electricity by source">Cost of electricity by source</a></div>
<p>Wind power is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_intensive" title="Capital intensive">capital intensive</a> but has no fuel costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRENA_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA-97">[96]</a></sup> The price of wind power is therefore much more stable than the volatile prices of fossil fuel sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> However, the estimated <a href="/wiki/Average_cost" title="Average cost">average cost</a> per unit of electric power must incorporate the cost of construction of the turbine and transmission facilities, borrowed funds, return to investors (including the cost of risk), estimated annual production, and other components, averaged over the projected useful life of the equipment, which may be more than 20 years. Energy cost estimates are highly dependent on these assumptions so published cost figures can differ substantially.
</p><p>The presence of wind energy, even when subsidized, can reduce costs for consumers (€5 billion/yr in Germany) by reducing the marginal price, by minimizing the use of expensive <a href="/wiki/Peaking_power_plant" title="Peaking power plant">peaking power plants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>The cost has decreased as wind turbine technology has improved. There are now longer and lighter wind turbine blades, improvements in turbine performance, and increased power generation efficiency. Also, wind project capital expenditure costs and maintenance costs have continued to decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021 a Lazard study of unsubsidized electricity said that wind power <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levelized_cost_of_energy" title="Levelized cost of energy">levelized cost of electricity</a> continues to fall but more slowly than before. The study estimated new wind-generated electricity cost from $26 to $50/MWh, compared to new gas power from $45 to $74/MWh.  The median cost of fully deprecated existing coal power was $42/MWh, nuclear $29/MWh and gas $24/MWh.  The study estimated offshore wind at around $83/MWh. <a href="/wiki/Compound_annual_growth_rate" title="Compound annual growth rate">Compound annual growth rate</a> was 4% per year from 2016 to 2021, compared to 10% per year from 2009 to 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incentives_and_community_benefits">Incentives and community benefits</span></h3>
<p>Turbine prices have fallen significantly in recent years due to tougher competitive conditions such as the increased use of energy auctions, and the elimination of subsidies in many markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> As of 2021 <a href="/wiki/Energy_subsidy" title="Energy subsidy">subsidies</a> are still often given to offshore wind. But they are generally no longer necessary for onshore wind in countries with even a very low carbon price such as China, provided there are no competing <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">fossil fuel subsidies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Secondary market forces provide incentives for businesses to use wind-generated power, even if there is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_Certificates" title="Renewable Energy Certificates">premium price for the electricity</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">socially responsible manufacturers</a> pay utility companies a premium that goes to subsidize and build new wind power infrastructure. Companies use wind-generated power, and in return, they can claim that they are undertaking strong "green" efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-green-e_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-green-e-103">[102]</a></sup> Wind projects provide local taxes, or payments in place of taxes and strengthen the economy of rural communities by providing income to farmers with wind turbines on their land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nine_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-nine-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>The wind energy sector can produce jobs during the construction and operating phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Jobs include the manufacturing of the wind mills, and the construction process which includes transporting, installing, and then maintaining these wind mills. An estimated 1.25 million people were employed in wind power in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Small-scale_wind_power">Small-scale wind power</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Small_wind_turbine" title="Small wind turbine">Small wind turbine</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Microgeneration" title="Microgeneration">Microgeneration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="451" decoding="async" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/220px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/330px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg/440px-Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quietrevolution_Bristol_3513051949.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A small <a href="/wiki/Quietrevolution_wind_turbine" title="Quietrevolution wind turbine">Quietrevolution QR5</a> <a href="/wiki/Gorlov_helical_turbine" title="Gorlov helical turbine">Gorlov type</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertical_axis_wind_turbine" title="Vertical axis wind turbine">vertical axis wind turbine</a> on the roof of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colston_Hall" title="Colston Hall">Colston Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol, England</a>. Measuring 3 m in diameter and 5 m high, it has a nameplate rating of 6.5 kW.</div></div></div>
<p>Small-scale wind power is the name given to wind generation systems with the capacity to produce up to 50 kW of electrical power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smallScaleCarbonTrust_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-smallScaleCarbonTrust-108">[107]</a></sup> Isolated communities, that may otherwise rely on <a href="/wiki/Diesel_generator" title="Diesel generator">diesel</a> generators, may use wind turbines as an alternative. Individuals may purchase these systems to reduce or eliminate their dependence on grid electric power for economic reasons, or to reduce their <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a>. Wind turbines have been used for household electric power generation in conjunction with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a> storage over many decades in remote areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>Examples of small-scale wind power projects in an urban setting can be found in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, where, since 2009, several building projects have capped their roofs with <a href="/wiki/Gorlov_helical_turbine" title="Gorlov helical turbine">Gorlov-type helical wind turbines</a>. Although the energy they generate is small compared to the buildings' overall consumption, they help to reinforce the building's 'green' credentials in ways that "showing people your high-tech boiler" cannot, with some of the projects also receiving the direct support of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Energy_Research_and_Development_Authority" title="New York State Energy Research and Development Authority">New York State Energy Research and Development Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>Grid-connected domestic wind turbines may use <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid energy storage</a>, thus replacing purchased electric power with locally produced power when available. The surplus power produced by domestic microgenerators can, in some jurisdictions, be fed into the network and sold to the utility company, producing a retail credit for the microgenerators' owners to offset their energy costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-home-made_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-home-made-111">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>Off-grid system users can either adapt to intermittent power or use batteries, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a>, or diesel systems to supplement the wind turbine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Equipment such as parking meters, traffic warning signs, street lighting, or wireless Internet gateways may be powered by a small wind turbine, possibly combined with a photovoltaic system, that charges a small battery replacing the need for a connection to the power grid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Distributed_generation" title="Distributed generation">Distributed generation</a> from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable resources</a> is increasing as a consequence of the increased awareness of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. The electronic interfaces required to connect renewable generation units with the <a href="/wiki/Utility" title="Utility">utility</a> system can include additional functions, such as active filtering to enhance the power quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ActiveFiltering_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-ActiveFiltering-114">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Airborne_wind_turbine" title="Airborne wind turbine">Airborne wind turbines</a>, such as kites, can be used in places at risk of hurricanes, as they can be taken down in advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_on_environment_and_landscape">Impact on environment and landscape</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1045330069" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="sidebar nomobile nowraplinks hlist"><tbody><tr><td class="sidebar-pretitle">Part of a series on</td></tr><tr><th class="sidebar-title-with-pretitle"><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy</a></th></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg"><img alt="Logo Renewable Energy by Melanie Maecker-Tursun V1 bgGreen.svg" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg/120px-Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg/180px-Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg/240px-Logo_Renewable_Energy_by_Melanie_Maecker-Tursun_V1_bgGreen.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
