</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_renewable_energy_topics_by_country" title="List of renewable energy topics by country">Topics by country</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">Marketing and policy trends</a></li></ul></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Renewable_energy_sources" title="Template:Renewable energy sources"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Renewable_energy_sources" title="Template talk:Renewable energy sources"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Renewable_energy_sources&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_wind_power" title="Environmental impact of wind power">Environmental impact of wind power</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/220px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/330px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg/440px-Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wb_deichh_drei_kuhs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">Livestock</a> grazing near a wind turbine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livestock_ignore_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-livestock_ignore-116">[115]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The environmental impact of wind power is minor compared to that of fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-117">[116]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPCC" title="IPCC">IPCC</a>, in assessments of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life-cycle_greenhouse-gas_emissions_of_energy_sources" title="Life-cycle greenhouse-gas emissions of energy sources">life-cycle greenhouse-gas emissions of energy sources</a>, wind turbines have a <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> value of 12 and 11 (<a href="/wiki/Gram" title="Gram">g</a>CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_equivalent" title="Carbon dioxide equivalent">eq</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KWh" title="KWh">kWh</a>) for offshore and onshore turbines, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Wind turbines have some of the lowest <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">global warming potential</a> per unit of electricity generated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-:9-120">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>Onshore (on-land) wind farms can have a significant visual impact and impact on the landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Due to a very low <a href="/wiki/Surface_power_density" title="Surface power density">surface power density</a> and spacing requirements, wind farms typically need to be spread over more land than other power stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grantham_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-grantham-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Their network of turbines, access roads, transmission lines, and substations can result in "energy sprawl";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energyfootprint_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-energyfootprint-6">[6]</a></sup>  although land between the turbines and roads can still be used for agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mar_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-mar-123">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> They also need to be built away from urban areas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> which can lead to "industrialization of the countryside".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Szarka_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Szarka-126">[125]</a></sup> Some wind farms are opposed for potentially spoiling protected scenic areas, archaeological landscapes and heritage sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> A report by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountaineering_Council_of_Scotland" title="Mountaineering Council of Scotland">Mountaineering Council of Scotland</a> concluded that wind farms harmed <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> in areas known for natural landscapes and panoramic views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Habitat loss and fragmentation are the greatest potential impacts on wildlife of onshore wind farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energyfootprint_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-energyfootprint-6">[6]</a></sup> But the worldwide ecological impact is minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-117">[116]</a></sup> Thousands of birds and bats, including rare species, have been killed by wind turbine blades,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> though wind turbines are responsible for far fewer bird deaths than fossil-fueled power stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> This can be mitigated with proper wildlife monitoring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many wind turbine blades are made of <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a> and some only had a lifetime of 10 to 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Argus_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Argus-134">[133]</a></sup> Previously, there was no market for recycling these old blades,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> and they were commonly disposed of in landfills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-136">[135]</a></sup> Because blades are hollow, they take up a large volume compared to their mass. Since 2019, some landfill operators have begun requiring blades to be crushed before being landfilled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Argus_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Argus-134">[133]</a></sup> Blades manufactured in the 2020s are more likely to be designed to be completely recyclable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-136">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wind turbines also generate noise. At a distance of 300 metres (980 ft) this may be around 45 dB, which is slightly louder than a refrigerator. At 1.5 km (1 mi) distance they become inaudible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> There are anecdotal reports of negative health effects on people who live very close to wind turbines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Peer-reviewed research has generally not supported these claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>The United States Air Force and Navy have expressed concern that siting large wind turbines near bases "will negatively impact radar to the point that air traffic controllers will lose the location of aircraft".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (April 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_government">Central government</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Setokazenooka-park01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="668" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/220px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/330px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Setokazenooka-park01.jpg/440px-Setokazenooka-park01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Setokazenooka-park01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Part of the <a href="/wiki/Seto_Windhill" title="Seto Windhill">Seto Hill Windfarm</a> in Japan.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">Nuclear power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_subsidies" title="Energy subsidies">subsidized by many governments</a>, and wind power and other forms of renewable energy are also often subsidized.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It has been suggested that a subsidy shift would help to level the playing field and support growing energy sectors, namely <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, wind power, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofuels" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-per_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-per-144">[143]</a></sup> History shows that no energy sector was developed without subsidies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-per_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-per-144">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> (IEA) (2011), energy subsidies artificially lower the price of energy paid by consumers, raise the price received by producers or lower the cost of production. "Fossil fuels subsidies costs generally outweigh the benefits. Subsidies to renewables and low-carbon energy technologies can bring long-term economic and environmental benefits".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Japanese_nuclear_accidents" title="2011 Japanese nuclear accidents">2011 Japanese nuclear accidents</a>, Germany's federal government is working on a new plan for increasing <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">renewable energy commercialization</a>, with a particular focus on offshore wind farms. Under the plan, large wind turbines will be erected far away from the coastlines, where the wind blows more consistently than it does on land, and where the enormous turbines won't bother the inhabitants. The plan aims to decrease Germany's dependence on energy derived from coal and nuclear power plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span></h3>
<p>Surveys of public attitudes across <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and in many other countries show strong public support for wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-com-147">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vipublic_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-vipublic-148">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eon_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-eon-149">[148]</a></sup>
In 2008, surveys found about 80% of EU citizens supported wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefacts_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefacts-150">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bakker et al. (2012) found in their study that residents who did not want turbines built near them suffered significantly more stress than those who "benefited economically from wind turbines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although wind power is a popular form of energy generation, onshore or near offshore wind farms are sometimes opposed for their impact on the landscape (especially scenic areas, heritage areas and archaeological landscapes), as well as noise, and impact on tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2007 survey of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Canada" title="Wind power in Canada">wind power in Canada</a>, 89% of respondents said that using renewable energy sources like wind or solar power was positive for Canada because these sources were better for the environment. Only 4 percent considered using renewable sources as negative since they could be unreliable and expensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup>
Another 2007 survey concluded that wind power was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">alternative energy</a> source most likely to gain public support for future development in Canada, with only 16% opposed to this type of energy. By contrast, 3 out of 4 Canadians opposed nuclear power developments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>In other cases, there is <a href="/wiki/Community_wind_energy" title="Community wind energy">direct community ownership of wind farms</a>. The hundreds of thousands of people who have become involved in Germany's small and medium-sized wind farms demonstrate such support there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2010 Harris Poll found strong support for wind power in Germany, other European countries, and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-com-147">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vipublic_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-vipublic-148">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>Public support in the United States has decreased from 75% in 2020 to 62% in 2021, with the Democrat Party supporting the use of wind energy twice as much as the Republican Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> President Biden has signed an executive order to begin building large scale wind farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, Shen et al. (2019) found that Chinese city-dwellers may be resistant to building wind turbines in urban areas, with a surprisingly high proportion of people citing an unfounded fear of radiation as driving their concerns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup>  Also, the study finds that like their counterparts in OECD countries, urban Chinese respondents are sensitive to direct costs and wildlife externalities. Distributing relevant information about turbines to the public may alleviate resistance.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community">Community</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Community_debate_about_wind_farms" title="Community debate about wind farms">Community debate about wind farms</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1172" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/450px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/675px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG/900px-Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_tubines_cumbria.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wind turbines such as these, in <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>, England, have been opposed for a number of reasons, including aesthetics, by some sectors of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Many wind power companies work with local communities to reduce environmental and other concerns associated with particular wind farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup>
In other cases there is <a href="/wiki/Community_wind_energy" title="Community wind energy">direct community ownership of wind farm projects</a>. Appropriate government consultation, planning and approval procedures also help to minimize environmental risks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-com-147">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup>
Some may still object to wind farms<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wind-watch.org_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-wind-watch.org-168">[167]</a></sup> but many say their concerns should be weighed against the need to address the threats posed by <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-:9-120">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> and the opinions of the broader community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the US, wind power projects are reported to boost local tax bases, helping to pay for schools, roads, and hospitals, and to revitalize the economies of rural communities by providing steady income to farmers and other landowners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nine_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-nine-104">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the UK, both the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust" title="National Trust">National Trust</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Campaign_to_Protect_Rural_England" title="Campaign to Protect Rural England">Campaign to Protect Rural England</a> have expressed concerns about the effects on the rural landscape caused by inappropriately sited wind turbines and wind farms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Whitelee_panorama.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1713" data-file-width="5371" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/450px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/675px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Whitelee_panorama.JPG/900px-Whitelee_panorama.JPG 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Whitelee_panorama.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panoramic view of the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Whitelee_Wind_Farm" title="Whitelee Wind Farm">Whitelee Wind Farm</a> with Lochgoin Reservoir in the foreground.</div></div></div>
<p>Some wind farms have become tourist attractions. The <a href="/wiki/Whitelee_Wind_Farm" title="Whitelee Wind Farm">Whitelee Wind Farm</a> Visitor Centre has an exhibition room, a learning hub, a café with a viewing deck and also a shop. It is run by the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Science_Centre" title="Glasgow Science Centre">Glasgow Science Centre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Denmark, a loss-of-value scheme gives people the right to claim compensation for loss of value of their property if it is caused by proximity to a wind turbine. The loss must be at least 1% of the property's value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Danish-loss-of-value-scheme_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Danish-loss-of-value-scheme-175">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite this general support for the concept of wind power in the public at large, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_effects_of_wind_power" title="Environmental effects of wind power">local opposition</a> often exists and has delayed or aborted a number of projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup>
As well as concerns about the landscape, there are concerns that some installations can produce excessive sound and vibration levels leading to a decrease in property values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> Potential broadcast-reception solutions include predictive interference modeling as a component of site selection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup>
A study of 50,000 home sales near wind turbines found no statistical evidence that prices were affected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>While aesthetic issues are subjective and some find wind farms pleasant and optimistic, or symbols of <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy independence</a> and local prosperity, protest groups are often formed to attempt to block some wind power stations for various reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wind-watch.org_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-wind-watch.org-168">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-183">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianQA_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardianQA-184">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some opposition to wind farms is dismissed as <a href="/wiki/NIMBY" title="NIMBY">NIMBYism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> but research carried out in 2009 found that there is little evidence to support the belief that residents only object to wind farms because of a "Not in my Back Yard" attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geopolitics">Geopolitics</span></h3>
<p>Wind cannot be cut off unlike oil and gas so can contribute to <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy security</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Turbine_design">Turbine design</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">Wind turbine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design" title="Wind turbine design">Wind turbine design</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wind-turbine_aerodynamics" title="Wind-turbine aerodynamics">Wind-turbine aerodynamics</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1034237262">.mw-parser-output .stack{box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .stack>div{margin:1px;overflow:hidden}@media all and (min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-left{float:left;clear:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-right{float:right;clear:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-left{float:left;clear:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-right{float:right;clear:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-left{float:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-right{float:right;margin-left:1em}}</style><div class="stack stack-right"><div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_turbine_int.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="314" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/220px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/330px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wind_turbine_int.svg/440px-Wind_turbine_int.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_turbine_int.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical wind turbine components: <div><ol><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Foundations" title="Wind turbine design">Foundation</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Connection_to_the_electric_grid" title="Wind turbine design">Connection to the electric grid</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Tower" title="Wind turbine design">Tower</a></li><li>Access ladder</li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Yawing" title="Wind turbine design">Wind orientation control (Yaw control)</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Nacelle_(wind_turbine)" title="Nacelle (wind turbine)">Nacelle</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Generator" title="Wind turbine design">Generator</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Anemometer" title="Anemometer">Anemometer</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Electrical_braking" title="Wind turbine design">Electric</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Mechanical_braking" title="Wind turbine design">Mechanical</a> Brake</li><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gearbox" title="Gearbox">Gearbox</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Blades" title="Wind turbine design">Rotor blade</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Pitch_control" title="Wind turbine design">Blade pitch control</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#The_hub" title="Wind turbine design">Rotor hub</a></li></ol></div></div></div></div>
</div><div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scout_moor_gearbox,_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/220px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/330px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/440px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scout_moor_gearbox,_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical components of a wind turbine (gearbox, rotor shaft and brake assembly) being lifted into position</div></div></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">Wind turbines</a> are devices that convert the wind's <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> into electrical power. The result of over a millennium of <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmill</a> development and modern engineering, today's wind turbines are manufactured in a wide range of horizontal axis and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertical_axis_wind_turbine" title="Vertical axis wind turbine">vertical axis</a> types. The smallest turbines are used for applications such as <a href="/wiki/Battery_charger" title="Battery charger">battery charging</a> for auxiliary power. Slightly larger turbines can be used for making small contributions to a domestic power supply while selling unused power back to the utility supplier via the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a>. Arrays of large turbines, known as <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farms</a>, have become an increasingly important source of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> and are used in many countries as part of a strategy to reduce their reliance on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.
</p><p>Wind turbine design is the process of defining the form and specifications of a <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbine</a> to extract energy from the <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">wind</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup>
A wind turbine installation consists of the necessary systems needed to capture the wind's energy, point the turbine into the wind, convert <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_energy" title="Mechanical energy">mechanical rotation</a> into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_power" title="Electrical power">electrical power</a>, and other systems to start, stop, and control the turbine.
</p><p>In 1919 the German physicist <a href="/wiki/Albert_Betz" title="Albert Betz">Albert Betz</a> showed that for a hypothetical ideal wind-energy extraction machine, the fundamental laws of conservation of mass and energy allowed no more than 16/27 (59%) of the kinetic energy of the wind to be captured. This <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betz%27_law" title="Betz' law">Betz limit</a> can be approached in modern turbine designs, which may reach 70 to 80% of the theoretical Betz limit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_aerodynamics" title="Wind turbine aerodynamics">aerodynamics of a wind turbine</a> are not straightforward. The airflow at the blades is not the same as the airflow far away from the turbine. The very nature of how energy is extracted from the air also causes air to be deflected by the turbine. This affects the objects or other turbines downstream, which is known as Wake effect. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Aerodynamics" title="Aerodynamics">aerodynamics</a> of a wind turbine at the rotor surface exhibit phenomena that are rarely seen in other aerodynamic fields. The shape and dimensions of the blades of the wind turbine are determined by the aerodynamic performance required to efficiently extract energy from the wind, and by the strength required to resist the forces on the blade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the aerodynamic <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Blade_design" title="Wind turbine design">design of the blades</a>, the design of a complete wind power system must also address the design of the installation's <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#The_hub" title="Wind turbine design">rotor hub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacelle_(wind_turbine)" title="Nacelle (wind turbine)">nacelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Tower" title="Wind turbine design">tower structure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_generator" title="Electric generator">generator</a>, controls, and foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_wind_power" title="History of wind power">History of wind power</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="739" data-file-width="714" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg/220px-Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg/330px-Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg/440px-Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_turbine_1888_Charles_Brush.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_F._Brush" title="Charles F. Brush">Charles F. Brush</a>'s windmill of 1888, used for generating electric power.</div></div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization#Wind_power" title="Renewable energy commercialization">Renewable energy commercialization § Wind_power</a></div>
<p>Wind power has been used as long as humans have put <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sailing_ships" title="Sailing ships">sails</a> into the wind. King Hammurabi's Codex (reign 1792 - 1750 BC) already mentioned windmills for generating mechanical energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> Wind-powered machines used to grind grain and pump water, the <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmill</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_pump" title="Wind pump">wind pump</a>, were developed in what is now <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> by the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> Wind power was widely available and not confined to the banks of fast-flowing streams, or later, requiring sources of fuel. Wind-powered pumps drained the <a href="/wiki/Polder#Polders_and_the_Netherlands" title="Polder">polders of the Netherlands</a>, and in arid regions such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_mid-west" title="American mid-west">American mid-west</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_outback" title="Australian outback">Australian outback</a>, wind pumps provided water for livestock and steam engines.
</p><p>The first windmill used for the production of electric power was built in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> in July 1887 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prof_James_Blyth" title="Prof James Blyth">Prof James Blyth</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anderson%27s_College" title="Anderson's College">Anderson's College</a>, Glasgow (the precursor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strathclyde_University" title="Strathclyde University">Strathclyde University</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price-196">[195]</a></sup> Blyth's 10 metres (33 ft) high cloth-sailed wind turbine was installed in the garden of his holiday cottage at <a href="/wiki/Marykirk" title="Marykirk">Marykirk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kincardineshire" title="Kincardineshire">Kincardineshire</a>, and was used to charge <a href="/wiki/Accumulator_(energy)" title="Accumulator (energy)">accumulators</a> developed by the Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Camille_Alphonse_Faure" title="Camille Alphonse Faure">Camille Alphonse Faure</a>, to power the lighting in the cottage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-Price-196">[195]</a></sup> thus making it the first house in the world to have its electric power supplied by wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> Blyth offered the surplus electric power to the people of Marykirk for lighting the main street, however, they turned down the offer as they thought electric power was "the work of the devil."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_196-2"><a href="#cite_note-Price-196">[195]</a></sup> Although he later built a wind turbine to supply emergency power to the local Lunatic Asylum, Infirmary, and Dispensary of <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Angus" title="Montrose, Angus">Montrose</a>, the invention never really caught on as the technology was not considered to be economically viable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price_196-3"><a href="#cite_note-Price-196">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p>Across the Atlantic, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">Cleveland, Ohio</a>, a larger and heavily engineered machine was designed and constructed in the winter of 1887–1888 by <a href="/wiki/Charles_F._Brush" title="Charles F. Brush">Charles F. Brush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> This was built by his engineering company at his home and operated from 1886 until 1900.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> The Brush wind turbine had a rotor 17 metres (56 ft) in diameter and was mounted on an 18 metres (59 ft) tower. Although large by today's standards, the machine was only rated at 12 kW. The connected dynamo was used either to charge a bank of batteries or to operate up to 100 <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">incandescent light bulbs</a>, three arc lamps, and various motors in Brush's laboratory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>With the development of electric power, wind power found new applications in lighting buildings remote from centrally generated power. Throughout the 20th century parallel paths developed small wind stations suitable for farms or residences. The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a> triggered the investigation in Denmark and the United States that led to larger utility-scale wind generators that could be connected to electric power grids for remote use of power. By 2008, the U.S. installed capacity had reached 25.4 gigawatts, and by 2012 the installed capacity was 60 gigawatts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> Today, wind-powered generators operate in every size range between tiny stations for battery charging at isolated residences, up to gigawatt-sized <a href="/wiki/List_of_offshore_wind_farms" title="List of offshore wind farms">offshore wind farms</a> that provide electric power to national electrical networks.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-minnesota-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-minnesota_62-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A study commissioned by the state of Minnesota considered penetration of up to 25%, and concluded that integration issues would be manageable and have incremental costs of less than one-half-cent ($0.0045) per kW·h.

 <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071201192029/http://www.puc.state.mn.us/docs/windrpt_vol%201.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Final Report – 2006 Minnesota Wind Integration Study"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. The Minnesota Public Utilities Commission. 30 November 2006. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.puc.state.mn.us/docs/windrpt_vol%201.pdf" rel="nofollow">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 1 December 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 January</span> 2008</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Final+Report+%E2%80%93+2006+Minnesota+Wind+Integration+Study&amp;rft.pub=The+Minnesota+Public+Utilities+Commission&amp;rft.date=2006-11-30&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.puc.state.mn.us%2Fdocs%2Fwindrpt_vol%25201.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWind+power"></span></span>
